This has been a banner year for the A.B. Weil Lodge. We have been involved in many successful community projects. We participated in the
Bell Ringer campaign for the Salvation Army at Christmas, a C.P.R. mannequin was donated to the Red Cross, convalescent cards were sent
to Jewish patients in local hospitals. We gave an award for outstanding service to a local policeman. Lastly, and most important, as our main
project for the year, we are donating a Torah to the Hillel House at Florida State University.

An important step in lodge growth was achieved with the merger of the Wolfson Lodge with our lodge this year. We are anxious to affiliate
all interested Jewish men in our fine organization.

Much of the success of this year was due to our President, Milton Hecht and the fine group of officers who worked closely with him. We
expect the upcoming year to be even more successful and once again urge all Jewish men to join and become active.

 

Jewish War Veterans

Lt. Meyer Leibov

The Hebrew Union Veterans (now Jewish War
Veterans) was founded as a direct result of slander
and insinuation that Jews had not participated in the
military during the Civil War. By 1860, however, Jews
had become an accepted part of the U. S. Military.

Jewish War Veterans maintains a strong united
front in Congress, making its voice heard on subjects
such as foreign policy, civil rights, defense spending,
veterans benefits, housing and education.

Through development of national positions on
these issues, J.W.V. helps to insure an effective demo-
cracy and the protection of our rights as Jews, Amer-
icans, and veterans. Hospital programs, veterans
and dependents rehabilitation, scouting, summer
camp scholarships, community activities - J.W.V.
involvement means a better life for everyone.

Every year J.W.V. Post No. 199 participates in the
Memorial Day ceremonies and in the Armistice Day
parade. This year, Memorial Day ceremonies took
place at 3 p.m. on Monday, May 29 at Evergreen
Cemetery. Colors of all veterans groups were pre-
sented and a wreath was laid.

Girl Scout Troop
No. 162

In the past year the members of Girl Scout Troop No. 162 took
part in many interesting activities. One of the highlights was a play
“A Treasure Without Measure” directed by Ellen Schnipper.
The play was the completion of requirements for the Troop
Dramatics badge. Our troop also participated in the Neighborhood
camping weekend at Camp Kateri. Those girls who attended earned
the Troop Camping badge. In addition to these two special events,
there were many craft projects including macrame, papier mache
and stitchery. We also worked on several requirements for other
badges. Several girls earned individual badges in addition to the
troop badges. One fun activity was baking refreshments in the
Center kitchen for Girl Scout Sabbath. The Girl Scouts and
Brownies participated in Friday Evening services for Girl Scout

Sabbath. Near the end of the year there was a Sunday afternoon
outing at the beach. The final activity was a swim party and cookout
with the Fly-up Ceremony for Brownies who will be going into the
Junior troop in the coming year. The members of the troop were:
Marion Bass, Lisa Greenspoon, Beverly Hyken, Irene Mann,
Melanie Proctor, Lesley Resnick, Elizabeth Schnipper and Jennifer
Warren. Clara Mann, Scout Leader

 

ALL ABOUT GIRL SCOUTS
by

Lisa Greenspoon

Girl Scouts consists of camping, earning badges, learning
new things, playing games and the cookie sale. But Girl Scouts is
more than that . . . it’s helping other people. The three things I liked
best were cooking, camping and the cookie sale.

Girl Scouts is a good experience for every girl. Learning new skills
is a lot of fun. We like to help people that need us. That is the most
important thing of all. I really enjoyed Girl Scouts this year.

 

ATID

ATID is the College Age Organization of Judaism sponsored by the United Synagogue of America. It was formed
and is led by college students and collegians who want to live and learn Judaism and continue their identification with
the Jewish Movement.

ATID invites all college age students who wish to involve themselves in Jewish life and thought.

Our Synagogue is very anxious to keep in touch with all of our youth throughout the year, so parents are urged to
contact the Center office and give us their address at school. Activities are planned during vacation periods to enable
our collegians to get together with their friends. During the Winter break last December, College age youth, under-
graduates, their families and friends shared the joy of Shabbat at special Shabbat Services in our Sanctuary. Our college
students participated in the services and the Dvar Torah and remarks were oriented to topics of their interest and
concerns.

Following the services the students were invited to an informal luncheonin their honor; to socialize and get-together .
... to sing, dance, enjoy the spirit of Shabbat and the renewed associations that they made. It is very important to
encourage our collegians to participate and “keep in touch”.

MINYANAIRE PROGRAM

The Jacksonville Jewish Center Minyanaires are dedicated to a program of prayer services, comraderie
as well as social and intellectual stimulation. A year of forums on contemporary social and religious issues
which affect the Jewish community and the community at large are being planned.

As part of its service to the health needs of the congregation, the Minyanaires in co-ordination with the
American Heart Association, sponsors C.P.R. classes (Cardiac-Pulmonary Resuscitation), and Blood Bank
Drives. 7

This Sunday morning program begins with minyan at 9:00 a.m. in the Witten Chapel, followed by break-
fast and the speaker of the-day. For information call Chairman, Gene Kornblum — 737-6127.

Standing outside Blood Bank Mobile Unit and anxiously awaiting
their turn are left to right; Abe Bielski, Jay Graff, Neil Sandler,
Julian Schneider shows no fear as he gives to protect his family. Gene Kornblum, Allen Gray, and Matt Frankel.

CENTER DAY CAMP

There are many camps and activities available for children during the
summer months, but only one Jewish Day Camp in the Jacksonville area.
The Center has felt the importance of continuingto make our excellent Camp
facilities available to all Jewish youth, giving them the opportunity to exper-
ience a wide variety of activities that promote physical, emotional and
spiritual growth encompassing the out-of-doors and nature.

An outstanding staff of specialists provide highly skilled and experienced
leadership ina wide variety of activities including: Judaica, Red CrossSwim
Instruction (as well as free swim), organized sports, arts and crafts, nature,
campcraft, canoeing, archery, tennis, overnight camping, drama, singing,
dancing and field trips.

Each summer includes four two-week sessions for campers between the
ages of five through twelve years, plus eight weekly half-day sessions for
campers three and four years of age. The camp fee is competitive with other
day camps, the program is more inclusive than most, with Jewish values
being an integral part of each day’s activities.

We look forward to many new concepts for the Day Camp 1979 and hope
that you will include our camp in the summer plans for your children.

 

Ron Weinberg - specialist
With Creative Craft Class.

David Moss

1884-1978

David Moss, Past President of the Jacksonville Jewish Center,
died at the age of 93 on June 15, 1978. He served as president
during 1926-1927, and again from 1937-1938. He devoted over 50
years of his life to the synagogue and the Jewish community, and
to the civic affairs of our city.

He was born in Punjest, Roumania, October 7, 1884, and
emigrated to America in 1904. At first he lived with relatives in
Savannah, Georgia and worked there for two years. In 1906 he
moved to Jacksonville. He was the first of six brothers and a sister
to arrive in America, and was instrumental in bringing each of them,
including his parents, to Jacksonville. In 1913 he married Fannie
Frank in Congregation B'nai Israel. They had one son, Norman.

He was actively involved in all areas of the Jewish community,
especially during the years of planning for the synagogue building
at 3rd and Silver Streets. During the 1920’s he participated in the
YMHA fund-raising and programming activities. In the late 1920’s he
was a member of the original group of men who formed what was
then known as the Jewish Welfare Society, and known now as the
Jewish Family and Children’s Services. He was later elected treasurer and served in that capacity for approximately 30 years.
In 1932 he was elected chairman of the Troop Committee of Boy Scout Troop No. 14, sponsored by the Jewish Center, and
served for 5 years.

In 1927 David Moss was selected as a member of the “National Committee of One Thousand” which was formed on the
occasion of the laying of the cornerstone of the Yeshiva College of America. In 1930 he was invited to become a member of the
National Advisory Council of the National Home for Jewish Children in Denver, Colorado.

During a visit to Memphis, Tennessee, in 1932, he observed a group of young people conducting their own services on
Shabbat. They called themselves a Junior Congregation. Upon his return to Jacksonville, he planned the formation of a Junior
Congregation at our synagogue. The success of this activity gave him much pleasure and satisfaction.

He was a life member of the Elks Club, and in 1943, during World WarII, he was chairman of the Scrap Metal Drive sponsored
by the Jacksonville Chamber of Commerce. He was also an active member of their Membership Committee, and received many
citations for his outstanding work. :

He worked for many years on the membership committee of the Zionist Organization of America. The Jewish National
Fund honored him for his untiring work by dedicating a forest in Israel in his name.

For many years he served as Treasurer of the Cemetery Committee, and was instrumental in purchasing the land now known
as the new cemetery at 44th street.

He was a man who loved and lived his Judaism.

 

By Norman Moss
Son of David Moss

The Jacksonville Jewish Center takes this occasion of the publication of this yearbook to mark indelibly in its records its appreciation and
indebtedness to David Moss for the permanent influence he left behind. One can list all of his accomplishments, but that is not sufficient.
David Moss cared for others, young and old alike, he had no preference. His happiness came from the happiness of others.

His dedication went beyondJacksonville . .. Israel was his love. Very few men can take the place of David Moss... many have benefitted from
his life and dedication to Judaism. He built our synagogue with years of hard work and frustration. But he persevered because he believed in
his religion and wanted Jacksonville to have a synagogue of which it could be proud. His dream became a reality . .. we are forever grateful.

potas:

This deed was found by Norman Moss, son of the late David Moss.
It dates back to 1924. We thank Norman for allowing us’to print it.

The Cemetery Committee provides a very necessary function of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. It is very important that
the Cemetery grounds are well kept and provide a peaceful resting place for our loved ones.

Our Cemetery Committee is co-chaired by Joe Becker and Jack Becker. Serving on their committee are Max Becker,
Herman Bloom, Eugene Henry, Hymie Selber, Alan Taffet, Sumner Waitz and Dr. Joe Witten.

Mr. Kenneth A. Bowden, Controller of the Jacksonville Jewish Center, also serves as general manager of our Cemetery. It
is his responsibility to oversee the upkeep and maintenance of the grounds. He has an excellent working relationship with Mr.
Jennewine who is general manager of Evergreen Cemetery. Mr. Jennewine has been very generous with his time and his
staff, Mr. Campbell, Mr. Miller and Mrs. Phillips. They have all taken excellent care of the Center’s property, above and beyond
what is expected. We appreciate everything they do.

Johnny B. Mercer has been custodian of our Cemetery for over 18 years. Mr. Bergeron of Southern Monument Co. has
always been extremely helpful to us too. Last year when our cemetery was vandalized, Mr. Bergeron came out, free of charge,
and repaired the monuments that were dislodged.

We are very grateful to all these people who have given so generously of their time. At this time we would like to mention the
names of David Moss and Sam Thier, of blessed memory, both of whom served on the Cemetery Committee for many years.
The Center family takes a great deal of pride in all the work they had done during their years of service on the committee.

Ws Editorial

I hope as you read this Yearbook that you will feel the same sense of
excitement and pleasure that I derived from putting it together. It has beena
challenging and rewarding experience. I would like to thank Sheldon
Gendzier and Hymie Selber for making it all possible. Raymond Cohen,
Irvin Ghelerter and George Strumlauf were my consultants and provided
me with their advice and expertise.

I would also like to thank Esther Fishler and Florence Robin, my dear
friends and my very understanding family, for their encouragement.

The Jacksonville Jewish Cente
===== PAGE 270 =====
BUR Cu RL)

 

As I look back on the past school years, Iam extremely grateful and pleased.
The Solomon Schechter Day School has grown from a Nursery and Kinder-
garten and First Grade to a full six grades. We have experienced many product-
ive years. The last school term was a most enjoyable and successful year.

The Solomon Schechter Day School has an innovative, bicultural curri-
culum of Hebrew learning and General Studies. The highly structured yet
individualized program in language arts, science and social studies, has been
developed by a skilled staff of instructors, resource personnel and university
consultants. Cultural field trips to the Museum of Arts and Sciences, the
Opera, Ballet, the Jacksonville Symphony and the Hayden Burns Library
enhance the child’s awareness of the world through observation, listening
and participation.

The Physical Education program is geared to the abilities of each child with
emphasis on sportsmanship and skill. Included in the program are swimming,

tennis, and small group games. The daily curriculum includes Hebrew language

instruction with a full program of Judaic-Hebrew learning experiences through
dance, song, art, role playing and prayer.

The Jacksonville Jewish Center Solomon Schechter Day School provides

all Jewish children in the community an outstanding General Studies education \

and a rich and rewarding Hebrew-Judaic education. The students of the day
school continually score high on achievement tests and have experienced much
success after leaving our school. This is all credited to a well-rounded program
and the creative atmosphere provided by the teachers, parents and the Educa-
tion Committee of the Center. Marilyn Sandler

 

,

Evelyn Borstein
School Secretary

 

Bs

Marilyn Sandler
Principal Solomon Schechter Day School

 

Suzi Roey
Assistant to the Administrator
of the Supplemental Schools

===== PAGE 271 =====
Third Grade Thespians

The 3rd Grade Class of the Solomon Sch-
echter Day School honored their mothers,
grandmothers, aunts and friends with a delight-
ful original play called “The Photo Album”
which was written by Mrs. Judy Reppert, the
3rd grade teacher. All who attended were de-
lighted with the entire program which consisted
of songs and poems along with adelicious lunch
which the children helped prepare. Mrs. Ilana
Manasse, the children’s Hebrew teacher, and
Mrs. Reppert added to the theme of children
growing up by having a contest to see if the
mothers could pick out the entire class from
their baby pictures. The mothers were present-
ed with photo albums of the class. These con-
tained pictures of the class from their baby stage
through their grown-up years. The children
dressed according to the time period of their
lives and the album was truly a work of art.

CHANUKAH PLAY; Top Row; Paul Hackel,
Miriam Mibab, Dina Levin, Karen Manassee,
Jeffrey Katz, Eileen Greenbaum, David Lazarus
Alyse Slaff, Manya Lazarus. Mid. Row; Jona-
JEWISH HEROS HALL OF - AME than Katz, Staci Ginsburg, Julie Sena, Kim Held

Front Row; Mrs.IlanaManasse Marc Selevan,
Eric Levy, Mrs. Judy Reppert.

This past year a very talented and creative group of third graders
and their teachers Judy Reppert and Ilana Manasse, put on many
plays and skits that tied in with their studies. Special thanks go to the
parents of these children for their co-operation.

Blanche Slott

Call the Center and ask for extension 457 and you will reach Blanche Slott. If she
answers she is probably busy in her office calculating costs for a Kiddush, a wedding,
reception or a Bar or Bat Mitzvah. Whatever your simcha, if it will take place at the
Center, Blanche will be involved one way or another. Food, waiters, tablecloths
and the like. You name it . . . Blanche is there, always ready to help you.

If you happen to call during the summer months, you will find Blanche at the Center
Day Camp where she has served as Director for 13 years. The campers affectionately
call her “Aunt Blanche”, and rightfully so. She has a special warmth that makes
each campter feel very much at home. The past few years she has worked very hard
to increase enrollment by hiring a highly-skilled staff. And it’s worked!

Blanche served as a volunteer at the Center for over 25 years before she joined the
staff of the Center as Activities Director. She was the first woman member on the
Board of Directors of the Jacksonville Jewish Center, where she served as‘Youth
Chairman. She is a past-president of Sisterhood and a former Girl Scout leader and
Den Mother. More recently she has been recognized for her artistic ability. Her‘works
have been on display at the Hayden Burns Library, local banks, and art shows all over
the southeast. She continues to share her expertise with youngsters after school on
Tuesdays and at the Sunday Funday Program.

We are very lucky to have Blanche Slott on the Center Staff. Her involvement with

youth, her sensitivity to the needs of the members and her devotion to the Center
cannot go unnoticed.

a

 

Children’s Tree of Life... Anew project of Sisterhood was very successful due to the efforts
of Ethel Krestul and Isabel Balotin. This tree will hang at all meetings. It is a felt appliqued
Tamarisk Tree with each leaf individually cut and embroidered. The response was so great
that another tree will be made.

The Sisterhood Closing Luncheon

The Sisterhood members that attended
this Luncheon had a very special treat.
Sylvia Weiner, assistant Curator of the
Jewish Museum in New York, gave a vivid
slide presentation of some of the treasurers
from the Museum’s collection. Just as
Judaism is more than areligion, The Jewish
Museum is more than a museum. Its role as
custodian of the collection of treasurers and
artifacts of the Jewish Peoples history is a
proud one, and its efforts to make the re-
sources of that heritage available to today’s
generations embrace a constantly expand-
ing variety of special programs. Pictured
with Sylvia Weiner are Horty Gendzier and
Sylvia Shorstein, Chairwomen of the day.

IADI

Goals and Objectives

Grades 7-8

y

 

Jewish families today look to the synagogue as the
center for Jewish activity: religious, educational,
social and recreational. A major goal of the syna-
gogue and its school is the education of youth witha
firm base of knowledge; Jewish identification; a
sense of pride in their heritage; and a commitment to
Judaism.

The goal of Kadima is to bring about the inter-
nalization of Jewish values, attitudes and behavior
patterns by supplementing the child’s formal reli-
gious education with informal Jewish learning
experience.

The objectives are simple:
® To recognize the importance of Shabbat and holiday
observance.
® To recognize the need for regular devotion both
individuatly_and in groups.
© To develop an appreciation of, and willingness to
work for the Synagogue.
®© To increase the use of Hebrew in informal settings.
® To establish a communal sense by supporting com-
munity and civic activities such as local charities,
Keren Ami, JNF.
© To recognize the importance of Israel as a modern
center for world Jewry.
© To develop a Jewish identity through music and
dance.
To develop an appreciation of Jewish Family life.
To understand the essential consonance of living as
an American and living as a Jew.

VIII

KADIMA

The Center is very grateful to Barbara and Eliot
Safer and Ava Hoffenberg who advised the Kadima
group this past year. Through their unselfish efforts
a very cohesive and exciting year was enjoyed by all
Kadimaniks.

This coming year is expected to be even more excit-
ing. Under the guidance of Rabbi Dov Kentof very
special programs have already been planned. If your
child is in the seventh or eighth grade call the Center
now. We are pleased to announce that Barbara and
Eliot Safer will continue as advisors.

Young Judea is the Zionist Youth Movement dedicated to instilling in our youth an appreciation
of our Jewish Heritage, ideals and values. Through youth organizations such as this, Jewish
children can get together in a relaxed atmosphere to discuss topics of interest, perform com-

munity services and socialize.

The Young Judeans that attended Camp Judea in Hendersonville, N.C. were Deborah Bressler,
Judy Bressler, Steven Cohan, Scott Panken, Melissa Roey, Shannon Sussman and Susan
Schwab. Marcia Greenbaum, who served as advisor of the Y oung Judeans this past year, worked
asa C.LT. along with Andrew Ruby at the camp. Ninth graders attended the National Young
Judea Camp, Tel Yehuda in Barryville, N.Y. If your child is in the fifth or sixth grade please

call Rabbi Dov Kentof at 268-6736.

On May 3, 1978 the Jacksonville Jewish Center along with all the Synagogues of the
Jacksonville Jewish Community held a memorial service and interfaith dialogue and program
observing Yom Hashoah (Holocaust Day).

 
 
 
 

The event was sponsored by the synagogues, Community Council and the National Council
of Christians and Jews. A very touching and inspiring program was experienced by all
those present.

 

Mrs. Phillip Freiden, Mrs. Chaim Bielski, Mrs: Jack Greenbaum, Rabbi David Gaffney, G.
Sigmund Raskin, Martin Tabak - - survivors of the Holocaust light candles in memory of the
six million Jews who perished.

 
 

 

A large crowd attends the memorial service at the Jewish Center to pay respect to the victims
of the Holocaust. Rabbi Gaffney leads the community in prayer.

TO OUR ADVERTISERS:

Our constant gratitude, not only for making the publication
possible, but also for the support they lend to our Youth
Activities. We urge our members to reciprocate with their
patronage.

e A reference and guide for the Jacksonville Jewish Center
membership and the Jewish community.

e Serves over 7,000 members and advertisers.
e All proceeds devoted to the Center’s program.

e The only Jewish publication in the community listing all
groups.

The Year Book is a summary of the various activities and
program of this Synagogue-Center depicted in pictures and
words. We are grateful to the many organizations of this
community who have cooperated in providing us with
material used.

We appreciate the efforts of our staff and other members of
the Center who have devoted time and effort on behalf of our
1978-79 Center Yearbook.

SIMHAT TORAH CELEBRATION —

WEDNESDAY, OCTOBER 5, 1977

CONGREGATION TO HONOR THREE LEADERS FOR OUTSTANDING SERVICE

The Festival of Sukkot reaches its joyous climax
on Simhat Torah, the last day of the Holiday. Simhat
Torah is the happiest holiday on the Jewish calendar
because we celebrate our joy and pleasure with the
Torah.

Because of Israel’s perennial love of the Torah,
it has been referred to in Jewish tradition as Israel’s
“bride.” A tradition. evolved in ancient times to honor
the individual called for the last reading of the Torah

—the Hatam Torah or the groom of the Torah. The
person honored to begin the Torah reading from its
beginning is called Hatam Bereshit the groom of
Genesis. We also honor a woman who has made a dis-
tinctive contribution to our Synagogue and to Jewish
life in general—the “Woman of Valor’ honor. We
will honor these individuals at Services on Simhat
Torah morning, Wednesday, October 5,

 

HARRY GENODZIER
Hatan Torah

Harry Gendzier will be honor-
ed as Hatam Torah, the groom of
the Torah. It is an honor truly
merited and deserved.

60 of Harry’s 80 years of life
have been spent in Jacksonville
Throughout the years he has been
a devoted and selfless leader con-
cerned with the multiple needs and
interests of the Jewish community.
Harry was a charter member of
the Hebrew Junior League which
helped to create he idea for the
Jacksonville Jewish Center. He is
a past President of the Jewish
Center and undoubtedly is pleased
to see this tradition carried on in
the person of his son Sheldon. Our

Hatan Torah was Chairman of the

Building Fund for 17 years and his
leadership was marked by dignity,
knowledge and by direction and
innovation.

Harry has served the Jewish com-
munity on a national basis as well.
He served as the President of the
Southeast Region of the United
Synagogue of America and was a

national Vice-President of the
United Synagogue. His years of
active involvement included distin-
guished service as President of
River Garden and President of the
Jacksonville Jewish Community
Council.

Members of his family and the
entire Jewish community is justly
proud of our “Groom of the Torah.”

 

SAMUEL ‘BUD" SHORSTEIN
Hatan Bereshit

Our Hatan Bershit (Bridegroom
of Genesis) this year is Bud Shor-
stein, a most deserved honor. Bud
has been serving as the Chairman
of our “Ein Breira” Building Cam-
paign during its period of greatest
challenge. It was Buddy’s dedica-
tion to the Center, initiative and
love for Jewish life that propelled
him to the forefront of this posi-
tion of responsibility. During his
chairmanship, the Center was able
to meet its wide ranging financial
responsibilities. Buddy’s leadership
and inspiration as an active Board
member has made it possible for
the Building Fund to achieve its
many objectives.

Mrs. Bess Shorstein, Buddy’s
mother, recalls our honoree’s love
for Judaism even at the tender age
of six. Buddy, dismissed from He-
brew School because he was too
young, returned the following day
with every determination to stay.
How lucky we are that he did. He
received his education at the Cen-
ter, was actively involved through
his teen years and continues to be
one of the Center’s bright leaders.

Buddy’s love and devotion to the
Jewish Center is a family affair. It
is said that he and his brother
Jack, our first Building Fund cam-
paign Chairman, are involved in
two partnerships, their accounting
practice and their unselfish dedi-
cation and devotion to the Jackson-
ville Jewish Center. We are proud
of Buddy and convey every best
wish for this most deserved honor.

 

MRS. LEO JACOBSON

"Woman of Valor”

The “Woman of Valor” honor
will be bestowed on Sheila Jacob-
son at Services this Simhat Torah.
Sheila, a tireless dynamo, has been
actively involved in the leadership
of the Jewish Center for many
years. As a co-chairperson of one
of the Center’s most important
committees, the Education Com-
mittee, Sheila has been in close
contact with every facet of the
wide ranging educational program
a the Center. Realizing that qual-
ity education will be possible only
if the necessary funds to make it
possible were available, our “Wo-
man of Valor” honoree assumed
the burden of fund raising for our
Solomon Schechter Day School.

Starting with the “Simcha 13”
affair which celebrated our Day
School’s Bar Mitzvah, Sheila has
consistently chaired every Day
School celebration and Raffle since
then with grace and elegance. Most
important her untiring and devot-
ed efforts have provided the neces-
sary funds to make possible the
quality of Jewish and general edu-
cation with which she is so con-
cerned. In her case, her love of
the synagogue and devotion to
Judaism is also a “family affair.”
Together with her husband Leo,
treasurer of the Jewish Center, and
her lovely family, the Jacobsons
are not only one of the most visible
of families—they are amongst the
vital families we have at the Center.

Services on Simhat Torah Wednesday, October 5
begin at 9:00 a.m. and will include the Hakafot Torah
Scroll Procession. A reception honoring Harry Gend-
zier, Samuel Shorstein and Mrs. Leo Jacobson will
be held immediately following Services.

The entire congregation extends heartfelt con-
gratulations to Harry and Belle Gendzier, the Shor-
stein family and Sheila and Leo Jacobson and their
families on this very special moment in their

lives.
